# The Reaver (Combat: Two-Handed)

The Reaver (Combat: Two-Handed)
CE Demon-Spawn Tiefling Vigilante 15


Strength: 16 (+2)  Dexterity: 12  Constitution: 14  Intelligence: 10 (-2)  Wisdom: 10  Charisma: 13 (+2)
Traits: Deadly Rush (Race) + dealer’s choice
Racial Traits: Maw or Claw, Fiendish Sprinter, Scaled Skin
Favored Class Bonuses: HP 1-20


Abilities


1: Dual identity, seamless guise, vigilante specialization (avenger), social talent (owl’s sight)
2: Vigilante talent (shield of blades)
3: Social talent (morphic mask), unshakable
4: Vigilante talent (heavy training)
5: Social talent (many guises), startling appearance
6: Vigilante talent (sweeping strike)
7: Social talent (quick change)
8: Vigilante talent (armor skin)
9: Social talent (skill familiarity)
10: Vigilante talent (close the gap)
11: Social talent (everyman), frightening appearance
12: Vigilante talent (mad rush)
13: Social talent (immediate change)
14: Vigilante talent (signature weapon: greatsword)
15: Social talent (mockingbird)


Feats


1: Power Attack (retrain at 2nd → Dirty Fighting)
2: Power Attack (shield of blades bonus)
3: Demonic Style
4: Heavy Armor Proficiency (heavy training bonus)
5: Improved Bull Rush
6: Cleave (sweeping strike bonus)
7: Demonic Momentum, Great Cleave (sweeping strike bonus)
8: 
9: Demonic Slaughter
10: 
11: Quick Bull Rush
12: 
13: Greater Bull Rush
14: Weapon Focus: Greatsword (signature weapon bonus), Weapon Specialization: Greatsword (signature weapon bonus)
15: Improved Critical: Greatsword


Strategy


Awww, everyone wants to play one of these builds at some point in their career, right? Absolutely zero subtlety, just rage and damage. The Reaver is predicated on the idea that you should ABC: A, always, B, be, C, charging. Always be charging. Always be charging. At low levels, this will be the whole strategy: activate Demonic Style for some attack and damage bonuses, charge an enemy with Power Attack on, and watch the damage numbers roll. (Don’t forget to use your bite attack from Maw or Claw! It’s a primary natural attack, so it’ll hit at your full BAB.) Levels 5-9 see some more interesting elements of the build come online. I’ve built you for bull rushing in this build, both because of how thematically cool it is for a raging tiefling descended from demons to toss enemies about the battlefield with ease and because Demonic Style requires it at later levels. Against squishy targets with low CMD scores, you can feel free to use Demonic Momentum to slam enemies back with a bull rush at the end of charge, then follow them to take advantage of your big damage bonuses on the following turn; Demonic Slaughter mitigates the loss of damage from bull rushing by allowing you to use Great Cleave whenever you succeed at your CMB check. Against tough or physically imposing enemies, best to stick with a normal charge, as the bull rush attempt won’t succeed consistently even with heavy investment.
The real boom sauce, however, comes into effect at 12th level with the mad rush vigilante talent. Mad rush allows you to paste a full-attack action onto the end of a charge—and that’s where Quick Bull Rush enters the scene. In place of one of your highest-BAB attacks (don’t worry—you’ve got haste and Maw or Claw) you get to bull rush an enemy as part of your full-attack! If this gambit works, you trigger a Great Cleave via Demonic Slaughter, immediately followed by the rest of your full-attack action—and all of these attacks, the Great Cleave, the full-attack, everything, snag the bonuses from both Demonic Style and Demonic Momentum. (Demonic Style specifies “melee attacks made as part of a charge,” which mad rush fulfills.) With those crazy attack and damage bonuses locked in, you’re incentivized to prey upon hordes of weaker enemies, knocking them around like nine pins and cutting them down en masse. The rest of the build is just devoted to making you harder to kill or facilitating charges: heavy training + armor skin + shield of blades is a classic Strength-based vigilante combo for strong-yet-mobile AC values, and close the gap both mitigates the AC penalty from charging and ensures that you can reach larger enemies without being cut to shreds. Sure-footed would be another great adjunct to this playstyle for charging through difficult terrain, but I opted for signature weapon at 14th level instead—your mileage may vary. At any rate, I really like this build, at least conceptually—anything founded on combat maneuvers is going to be a little shaky sooner or later, but you can always fall back on full-attacking enemies with mad rush, even if your bull rushes never work out.
________________

---

# The Bladecatcher (Combat: Sword and Board)

The Bladecatcher (Combat: Sword and Board)
NG Human Vigilante 15


Strength: 15 (+2)  Dexterity: 13  Constitution: 14  Intelligence: 10  Wisdom: 10  Charisma: 14
Traits: Dealer’s choice + dealer’s choice
Racial Traits: N/A
Favored Class Bonuses: Seamless guise 1-20


Abilities


1: Dual identity, seamless guise, vigilante specialization (avenger), social talent (owl’s sight)
2: Vigilante talent (shield of fury)
3: Social talent (social grace), unshakable
4: Vigilante talent (take ‘em alive)
5: Social talent (many guises), startling appearance
6: Vigilante talent (heavy training)
7: Social talent (quick change)
8: Vigilante talent (steel soldier)
9: Social talent (skill familiarity)
10: Vigilante talent (fist of the avenger)
11: Social talent (everyman), frightening appearance
12: Vigilante talent (mad rush)
13: Social talent (immediate change)
14: Vigilante talent (close the gap)
15: Social talent (hidden magic)


Feats


1: Power Attack, Weapon Focus: Spiked Gauntlet (human bonus)
2: Improved Shield Bash (shield of fury bonus)
3: Shield Gauntlet Style
4: 
5: Shielded Gauntlet Attack
6: Two-Weapon Fighting (shield of fury bonus), Heavy Armor Proficiency (heavy training bonus)
7: Shielded Gauntlet Master
8: 
9: Improved Two-Weapon Fighting
10: Improved Unarmed Strike (fist of the avenger bonus)
11: Double Slice
12: 
13: Two-Weapon Rend
14: 
15: Greater Two-Weapon Fighting


Strategy


This chicanery of a build is founded on the unnaturally strong interaction between Shield Gauntlet Style and the steel soldier vigilante talent, and gets you all the melee blender-style combat you could want while also sporting pretty fantastic AC numbers and surprisingly economical attribute allocations. Let’s jump in!
For starters, you’ll notice that much of this build is a pretty boilerplate Two-Weapon Fighting sword-and-board build with heavy armor. But from 2nd to about 10th level, everything about this build takes a fun left turn, and that starts with Shield Gauntlet Style at 3rd level. What this feat does is allow you to treat a spiked gauntlet as though it were a buckler. Simple enough, right? Under normal circumstances, you wouldn’t be able to shield bash or do anything other than wield your gauntlet if you wanted to receive its shield bonus to AC, but shield of fury (which comes online at 2nd level) permits you to shield bash with a gauntlet if you really wanted to. (You won’t, at this level, as your main hand weapon will do far more damage.) Take ‘em alive at 4th level will start to rack up the all-important bonuses to attack and damage whenever you deal nonlethal damage, and Shielded Gauntlet Attack at 5th level will give you better damage dice than you would normally enjoy on your punchy-punchy attacks, but this build doesn’t truly start to emerge until 6th to 8th, when something very important happens each level.
At 6th, shield of fury finally grants you Two-Weapon Fighting, as long as one of the weapons you’re using is a shield. No problem! Shield Gauntlet Style turns our gauntlet into a buckler for those purposes. You’ll now be able to take three attacks in a full-attack action, two with your main hand weapon and one with your off-hand buckler. At 7th level, Shielded Gauntlet Master comes online. Although this would technically allow you to wield two manufactured weapons and a gauntlet, we’re mostly interested in the fact that your gauntlet’s weapon enhancement bonus is also treated as its shield enhancement bonus. But don’t enchant it yet! Don’t do anything until 8th level, when the steel soldier vigilante talent lays down the final puzzle piece: when wearing your modified armor, you treat your armor’s enhancement bonus as its weapon enhancement bonus. What this does is spread your armor enhancement costs over three domains: if you’re wearing +4 hellknight plate, you’ll get the +4 enhancement bonus to your armor from its base enchantments, but also a +4 enhancement bonus to your gauntlet’s weapon attack and damage rolls (steel soldier) that then gets transferred again to your gauntlet’s shield enhancement bonus (Shielded Gauntlet Master). In essence, every point of investment in your armor’s enhancement bonus grants +1 attack, +1 damage, and +2 AC. How’s that for economy?
But wait! Who says you need to wield any other weapon in your main hand at all? I mean, yeah, technically this is a sword and board build, but you’re already not wielding a board, so why not ditch the sword, too? The wording in Shielded Gauntlet Style is somewhat ambiguous, but my interpretation is that a main hand gauntlet is also acceptable, but only the gauntlet in your off-hand counts as a buckler. That’s fine! If you wield two spiked gauntlets, each will inherit the armor’s enhancement bonuses to attack and damage (steel soldier), each will inherit sacred weapon’s scaling damage dice (Shielded Gauntlet Attack), and one will inherit its weapon enhancement bonuses as shield enhancement bonuses (Shielded Gauntlet Master). Once fist of the avenger drops at 10th level, each attack will pick up a +5 damage bonus on every hit. Double Slice at 11th lets you use your full Strength modifier with your off-hand, Two-Weapon Rend at 13th grants another quasi-attack, and finally Greater Two-Weapon Fighting at 15th grants yet another attack. Assuming you’ve picked up +5 armor and have a Strength score of ~24, at 15th level you’ll deal an average of 228.5 damage on a full-attack charge (thanks, mad rush and close the gap!) if all your attacks hit. It’s worth being judicious with Power Attack in this build, because your attack bonuses are already lowered from Two-Weapon Fighting and your Power Attack damage bonuses are already lowered from not two-handing a weapon. Only turn on Power Attack when you’re beating down a minion—it’s better to take +31/+31/+26/+26/+21/+21 (plus Two-Weapon Rend) and hit with most of your iteratives for an average of 180.5 damage than it is to go for +27/+27/+22/+22/+17/+17 and miss with most of your iteratives.
________________

---

# The Gauntlet (Combat: Unarmed)

The Gauntlet (Combat: Unarmed)
LG Angelkin Aasimar Unchained Monk (Scaled Fist) 1 / Vigilante 14


Strength: 16 (+2)  Dexterity: 12  Constitution: 14  Intelligence: 8  Wisdom: 10  Charisma: 14 (+2)
Traits: Martial Artist (Regional) + dealer’s choice
Racial Traits: Scion of Humanity
Favored Class Bonuses: Seamless guise 1-20


Abilities


1: Flurry of blows, AC bonus, draconic might
2(1): Dual identity, seamless guise, vigilante specialization (avenger), social talent (social grace), social grace (Diplomacy)
3(2): Vigilante talent (take ‘em alive)
4(3): Social talent (renown), unshakable
5(4): Vigilante talent (heavy training)
6(5): Social talent (feign innocence), social grace (Bluff), startling appearance
7(6): Vigilante talent (fist of the avenger)
8(7): Social talent (great renown)
9(8): Vigilante talent (armor skin)
10(9): Social talent (triumphant return), social grace (Sense Motive)
11(10): Vigilante talent (shield of blades)
12(11): Social talent (incredible renown), frightening appearance
13(12): Vigilante talent (mad rush)
14(13): Social talent (instant recognition)
15(14): Vigilante talent (close the gap)


Feats


1: Power Attack, Dragon Style (monk bonus), Improved Unarmed Strike (monk bonus), Stunning Fist (monk bonus)
2(1): 
3(2): Enforcer
4(3): 
5(4): Dragon Ferocity
6(5): 
7(6): Hurtful
8(7): 
9(8): Improved Initiative
10(9): 
11(10): Signature Skill: Intimidate
12(11): 
13(12): Great Fortitude
14(13): 
15(14): Furious Focus


Strategy


        Did I build Batman? Yeah, I kinda built Batman. We can quibble about whether Batman is properly an avenger or a stalker—I think there’s a case to be made for either—another time, because right now it’s time to talk about mashing face as an unarmed vigilante. This build combines roughly four elements: (1) great unarmed strike damage, (2) heavy armor and good AC values, (3) a surprising amount of mobility, and (4) the basics of a demoralization build. Moving in order, Power Attack is obviously a must, and flurry of blows + fist of the avenger + take ‘em alive will give us a combined +5 to unarmed attack rolls and +10 to unarmed damage rolls with an extra attack as a cherry on top. Dragon Style and Dragon Ferocity are mostly present to multiply our static Strength modifier, although they have excellent benefits for saves and mobility, as well. Later in the build, the mad rush vigilante talent ensures that you basically never spend a turn not full-attacking. Moving on to defenses, heavy training is obviously a good place to start, but if you wanted to do a much more bare-bones build, say, to focus a bit more on offense, you could always ditch heavy training and armor skin in favor of a wand of mage armor plus the scaled fist’s Charisma bonus to AC. At any rate, you’ll pick up shield of blades at 11th level, which is another evergreen source of AC.
        Mobility: you have a lot of it, somehow! Armor skin is a great vigilante talent for ensuring that you can run, jump, sneak, etc. while still wearing your full plate, but the real star of the show is Dragon Style, which grants a host of benefits to improve your ability to charge at enemies. Once you reach mad rush at 13th level, you should always close with enemies by charging, and can even mitigate the AC penalty with close the gap and shield of blades. Finally, we’ve got the essentials for an Intimimancy build here, including Enforcer and Signature Skill: Intimidate. There’s nothing very special that you need to do to trigger this part of the build—simply attack using nonlethal damage (you’d be doing this to proc take ‘em alive anyway, Batman) and roll Intimidate checks whenever needed. I’m fond of cruel handwraps for this build, since they’ll allow you to both demoralize and sicken enemies when you punch them. The many renown social talents should keep your Intimidate scores relevant with fairly minimal investment, but you’ll likely want to have full ranks in the skill by 11th level, when Signature Skill: Intimidate opens up a whole new can of whoop-ass on enemies. 10 ranks is when you start becoming able to dole out the panicked condition, so this is your cue to start peeling enemies off of large fights by scaring the living daylights out of them. Remember what Ra’s al Ghul taught you: fear is a weapon.
________________

---

# The Oni (Combat: Natural Attacks)

The Oni (Combat: Natural Attacks)
LE Human Unchained Monk (Scaled Fist) 1 / Vigilante (Chu Ye Enforcer) 14


Strength: 12  Dexterity: 16 (+2)  Constitution: 12  Intelligence: 8  Wisdom: 10  Charisma: 15
Traits: Martial Artist (Regional) + dealer’s choice
Racial Traits: N/A
Favored Class Bonuses: Seamless guise 2-20


Abilities


1: Flurry of blows, AC bonus, draconic might
2(1): Hidden strike +1d8, dual identity, seamless guise, yokai heart, oni mask, steel dictate, vigilante specialization (stalker)
3(2): Vigilante talent (lethal grace)
4(3): Hidden strike +2d8, social talent (social grace), unshakable
5(4): Deceitful form
6(5): Hidden strike +3d8, social talent (seamless shapechanger), startling appearance
7(6): Deadly horns
8(7): Hidden strike +4d8, social talent (quick change)
9(8): Vigilante talent (take ‘em alive)
10(9): Hidden strike +5d8, social talent (skill familiarity)
11(10): Vigilante talent (strike the unseen)
12(11): Hidden strike +6d8, social talent (many guises), frightening appearance
13(12): Third eye
14(13): Hidden strike +7d8, social talent (immediate change)
15(14): 


Feats


1: Weapon Finesse (retrain at 3rd → Weapon Focus: Unarmed Strike), Weapon Focus (human bonus), Combat Reflexes (monk bonus), Improved Unarmed Strike (monk bonus), Stunning Fist (monk bonus)
2(1): 
3(2): Dazzling Display, Weapon Finesse (lethal grace bonus)
4(3): 
5(4): Enforcer
6(5): 
7(6): Improved Initiative
8(7): 
9(8): Shatter Defenses
10(9): 
11(10): Disheartening Display, Blind-Fight (strike the unseen bonus), Improved Blind-Fight (strike the unseen bonus)
12(11): 
13(12): Signature Skill: Intimidate
14(13): 
15(14): Multiattack


Strategy


I wanted a natural attack build that used the Chu Ye enforcer archetype, and I got my wish! Once you understand how the archetype’s polymorph abilities fit together, this build is actually pretty straightforward: you’ll generally start off with a Dazzling Display to demoralize enemies, close with the one you want to beat up, then start full-attacking. You’ll have your flurry of blows made as kicks, followed by four natural attacks (claw, claw, bite, horns) from Chu Ye enforcer. If even one attack hits, the enemy becomes flat-footed against all the rest of your attacks, allowing you to trigger your hidden strike damage repeatedly; I’d recommend cruel handwraps and armor with the malevolent enchantment to take advantage of all the nastiness that demoralization can leverage. By 15th level, you’ll be able to assume giant form I more or less at will during combat, and will have Signature Skill: Intimidate, Disheartening Display, and Multiattack to further amp up the pain on enemies. Not particularly nuanced as a build, but undeniably effective.
________________
